    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

<div id="descriptionContainer">
  
      <div id="description" class="readable stacked" style="right:0">
        
<span id="freeTextContainer4715310309444582715">Fantastic Mr. Fox is on the run! The three meanest farmers around are out to get him. Fat Boggis, squat Bunce, and skinny Bean have joined forces, and they have Mr. Fox and his family surrounded. What they don’t know is that they’re not dealing with just any fox–Mr. Fox would never surrender. But only the most fantastic plan ever can save him now.</span>

      </div>
</div>

You like foxes and I think you will like it :). <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>

<div id="review_1022649516" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1022649516" />
    <a title="Patrick" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/922495-patrick"><img alt="Patrick" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1351307095p2/922495.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1022649516?book_show_action=true">Aug 10, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Patrick" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Patrick" href="/user/show/922495-patrick">Patrick</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1022649516" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7152530213169386126">My impressions in a single word: Meh. <br/><br/>I recently read this to my little boy, and I have to admit I really didn't care for it. <br/><br/>Don't get me wrong. It's not a *terrible* book. There's nothing hideously wrong with it. (See my review of Esio Trot, if you want to see me go off on a Dahl book I hated.) <br/><br/>But there wasn't much right with it either. The simple fact was Mr. Fox was not, in fact, very fantastic. <br/><br/>The plot centers around some farmers that try to kill Mr. Fox. They try to dig him out of his ho</span>
  <span id="freeText7152530213169386126" style="display:none">My impressions in a single word: Meh. <br /><br />I recently read this to my little boy, and I have to admit I really didn't care for it. <br /><br />Don't get me wrong. It's not a *terrible* book. There's nothing hideously wrong with it. (See my review of Esio Trot, if you want to see me go off on a Dahl book I hated.) <br /><br />But there wasn't much right with it either. The simple fact was Mr. Fox was not, in fact, very fantastic. <br /><br />The plot centers around some farmers that try to kill Mr. Fox. They try to dig him out of his hole. Fox's clever solution? Dig down so they can't reach him. <br /><br />But then the farmers dig *faster.*<br /><br />Fox's clever solution? They should dig away faster.<br /><br />Eventually they try to starve Mr. Fox and his family out of the hole. <br /><br />Fox's clever solution? Dig even farther and steal some food. <br /><br />And that's pretty much the whole book. (Spoiler alert.) <br /><br />I like my books to have some cleverness in them. If you have a book where the main character is a Fox, and people are going to praise him for being fantastic, he better... y'know... do something if not fantastic, then at least interesting. <br /><br />If your clever solution to *every* problem is "Dig more" you're kinda just phoning it in. <br /><br />Also some mild sexism in here. Nothing horrifying like in Esio Trot, but why read a meh book with mild sexism to your kids? There's better stuff out there. Much better.</span>
  <a data-text-id="7152530213169386126" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3073622434" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer694031431215831725">Fantastic Mr. Fox, Roald Dahl<br/>Fantastic Mr Fox is a children's novel written by British author Roald Dahl. It was published in 1970. The story revolves around an anthropomorphic, tricky, and clever fox named Mr. Fox who lives underground beside a tree with his wife and four children. In order to feed his family, he makes night visits to farms owned by three wicked, rude, cruel and dim-witted farmers named Boggis, Bunce and Bean and snatches away the livestock available on each man's farm. Tired o</span>
  <span id="freeText694031431215831725" style="display:none">Fantastic Mr. Fox, Roald Dahl<br />Fantastic Mr Fox is a children's novel written by British author Roald Dahl. It was published in 1970. The story revolves around an anthropomorphic, tricky, and clever fox named Mr. Fox who lives underground beside a tree with his wife and four children. In order to feed his family, he makes night visits to farms owned by three wicked, rude, cruel and dim-witted farmers named Boggis, Bunce and Bean and snatches away the livestock available on each man's farm. Tired of being outsmarted by Mr. Fox, the farmers devise a plan to ambush him as he leaves his burrow, but they succeed only in shooting off his tail. The farmers then dig up the Foxes' burrow using spades and then excavators. The Foxes manage to escape by burrowing further beneath the earth to safety. The trio of farmers are ridiculed for their persistence but they refuse to give up and vow not to return to their farms until they have caught Mr. Fox. They then decide to surround Mr. Fox's hole and wait until he is hungry enough to come out. Cornered by their enemies, Mr. Fox and his family, and all the other underground creatures that lived around the hill, begin to starve. ...<br /><br />عنوانها: آقای روباه شگفت‌ انگیز؛ آقا روباه شگفت‌انگیز؛ آقای فاکس رویایی و داستان داروی حیرت‌ انگیز جرج و داستان کشیش نیبلزویک؛ جناب روباه شگفت‌انگیز؛ روباه حیله‌ گر؛ روباه زرنگ؛ روباه فوق‌العاده؛ نویسنده: رولد دال؛ تاریخ نخستین خوانش: روز پنجم ماه دسامبر سال 2010 میلادی<br /><br />عنوان: آقای روباه شگفت‌ انگیز؛ نویسنده: رولد دال؛ مترجم: محبوبه نجف‌خانی؛ تهران: افق، واحد کودک، کتابهای فندق‏‫، 1388؛ در 136 ص، مصور، شابک: 9789643695910؛ چاپ دوم 1390؛ چاپ سوم 1391؛ چاپ دیگر: تهران: نشر افق، کتابهای فندق‏‫، 1392؛ در 124 ص؛ چاپ ششم 1392؛ چاپ هفتم 1393؛ چاپ هشتم و نهم 1395؛ موضوع: داستانهای نویسندگان نروژی تبار بریتانیایی -   <span id="freeText5619702702055567002" style="display:none">It turns out that my kid and I are both Dahl fans. Not uber-fans, but we usually always have a pretty good time every time we crack a book.<br /><br />THIS IS A GOOD THING. We didn't have that great a time with Narnia. Give us Gaiman, give us Dahl, and even give us Dickens, but Please, No Thank You to Lewis. :)<br /><br />High points of Mr. Fox:<br /><br />The bad guys look and sound not like farmers, but bankers. We have a full redistribution of wealth scheme going on here... maybe not so much Communism as it is a garden variety Socialist societal setup told within a simple tale digging holes and getting one's tail shot off.<br /><br />Fortunately, it's not THAT dry. In fact, I was pretty amused to see just how much hard liquor is downed by all. I mean, it's not just theft and murder we're talking about -- but the full-on drunken debaucheries of the proletariat... FOR the proletariat!<br /><br />Read it if you don't believe me. :) <br /></span>

<div id="review_63215206" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/63215206" />
    <a title="Greg" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/42508-greg"><img alt="Greg" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1368721201p2/42508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/63215206?book_show_action=true">Jul 12, 2009</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Greg" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Greg" href="/user/show/42508-greg">Greg</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142410349" href="/book/show/109008.Fantastic_Mr_Fox">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=foxes">foxes</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/42508-greg?shelf=books-for-kids">books-for-kids</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer63215206" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13546101795771753723">Mr. Fox steals food nightly from one of the three disgusting and gluttonous farmers who have more then they need. The farmers get mad and set out to kill Mr. Fox. They have a hard time catching him, they destroy the earth trying to get him out of his hole, they waste many man-hours by making their workers surround the woods with weapons and ultimately Mr. Fox with the help of other underground animals find another way into the farms and go about their stealing in peace while the farmers sit endl</span>
  <span id="freeText13546101795771753723" style="display:none">Mr. Fox steals food nightly from one of the three disgusting and gluttonous farmers who have more then they need. The farmers get mad and set out to kill Mr. Fox. They have a hard time catching him, they destroy the earth trying to get him out of his hole, they waste many man-hours by making their workers surround the woods with weapons and ultimately Mr. Fox with the help of other underground animals find another way into the farms and go about their stealing in peace while the farmers sit endlessly waiting to kill the fox and any other animals that pop up from the ground. <br /><br />This book teaches you that stealing is ok, as long as it is done against evil and wicked people. That's a fine message and one that kids probably won't be exposed to for the first time by reading this book. Basically Robin Hood is that message too, although this seems a little bit more anarchic in it's presentation, maybe it's the drawings, or all the fun the fox has in stealing that makes it seem like a revolution going on that you can dance to. <br /><br />But is it ok to tell kids that stealing is alright? Yes it is. Children will be taught eventually in school that stealing is perfectly fine, but they will be taught it under the more civilized and devastating guise of capitalism, the rights of corporations over people and the other legalized theft that our society holds up as the makings of success. But am I saying that kids should go out and steal? No they shouldn't. First because most of them are really bad at it and if you are bad at stealing you will get caught, or at least noticed and that's not a good thing. Second because stealing for the sake of stealing isn't good. Stealing can be political and it can be used as a very very weak brick against the wall of capitalism (but really it's more like throwing a feather into a tornado, it's not going to do shit), but it can also just be selfish and unnecessary. I was going to write more, but I'm running out of time before I goto work and see if I can spy any shoplifters, who I will try to have get caught because a) they make my life more difficult, in that I need to then remember what books have numbers off so they can be ordered manually, and a.2) mean that it gives reason for me to get yelled at by some idiot who can't understand just because the computer says we have something doesn't mean we really do (we don't have computers that know when someone has stolen something without our noticing it). And b) because the publishing industry has enough problems right now with money, and it's not as if books aren't available for free at libraries. Go there and get the book for free and read it, B&amp;N might be an big corporation, but as Ralph Nader said, (not an exact quote) "they sell books, and books are a good thing". <br /><br />So if you're going to go steal, go to some Wal-Mart or something, but watch out they have a wall of video screens in the back room with a small army watching them, just waiting to see you pocket some of their items. </span>
  <a data-text-id="13546101795771753723" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Trish" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3461034-trish"><img alt="Trish" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1588663568p2/3461034.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1495441460?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Trish" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Trish" href="/user/show/3461034-trish">Trish</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141346441" href="/book/show/17242192-fantastic-mr-fox">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1495441460" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6733294978245216111">This morning two new Roald Dahl books arrived and this one was an instant must-read. From a young age on I always adored stories about forest animals (which is why it's even more incomprehensible and outrageous that I have missed out on such a classic until now)!<br/><br/>The book is very thin but the story inside is full of wit, fun and excitement!<br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452172780i/17655883._SY540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Roald Dahl tells the story of Mr. Fox, his wife and children and their tranquil life. However, there are 3 farmers with very bad intentions and since Mr. Fox i</span>
  <span id="freeText6733294978245216111" style="display:none">This morning two new Roald Dahl books arrived and this one was an instant must-read. From a young age on I always adored stories about forest animals (which is why it's even more incomprehensible and outrageous that I have missed out on such a classic until now)!<br><br>The book is very thin but the story inside is full of wit, fun and excitement!<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452172780i/17655883._SY540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Roald Dahl tells the story of Mr. Fox, his wife and children and their tranquil life. However, there are 3 farmers with very bad intentions and since Mr. Fox is trying to save his family, he must be very clever indeed and come up with a fantastic plan - which he does.<br><br>The story unfolds in a very thrilling way (not too bloody though, clearly because it's meant for smaller children too) and the author managed to put some moral concepts even in here (in this case it's about stealing and catch &amp; release).<br>What I especially love is that the author shows a clever fox but not a malicious one. His characterization is entirely amiable (which is not always the case with stories about foxes).<br><br>As with the other volumes, this one also features lots and lots of illustrations by Quentin Blake and I think they will never lose their magic.<br>So if the three farmers haven't died, they are still waiting! *lol*<br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1452172780i/17655884._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6733294978245216111" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText3901716763841929489" style="display:none"><i>“ The finest and fattest ducks and geese, plucked and ready for roasting! And up above, dangling from the rafters, there must have been at least a hundred smoked hams and fifty sides of bacon!”</i><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1572877281i/28400679._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>While in the process of reading or re-reading Roal Dahl's wonderful works, this is the first book which doesn't agree with my taste. The interesting thing is that I remember watching the movie and not liking it either. It must be that something about this story, or maybe about Mr. Fox as a character, just isn't for me.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1572877281i/28400680.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>Or <i>maybe</i> it's the fact that the message of this book (a kids' book!!!), if put in a few words, is this: if you want to succeed in life and become a fantastic fox/being, just steal, insult people, and drink underage! A recipe for success. I guess...? 🤔</span>
  <a data-text-id="3901716763841929489" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1133054189" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1133054189" />
    <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks"><img alt="Stacey (prettybooks)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577577052p2/3533262.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1133054189?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stacey (prettybooks)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stacey (prettybooks)" href="/user/show/3533262-stacey-prettybooks">Stacey (prettybooks)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142410349" href="/book/show/109008.Fantastic_Mr_Fox">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics-challenge">classics-challenge</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=classics">classics</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=read-in-my-twenties">read-in-my-twenties</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3533262-stacey-prettybooks?shelf=childrens-fiction">childrens-fiction</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1133054189" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10267164793033300954"><i>This is a short blogpost taken from <a href='http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/16/thoughts-on-roald-dahl-the-bfg-the-witches-fantastic-mr-fox/' rel='nofollow noopener'>Thoughts on Roald Dahl: The BFG, The Witches & Fantastic Mr. Fox</a>.</i><br/><br/>I wasn't sure why, but <em>Fantastic Mr. Fox</em> felt the most <em>festive</em> to me, so I thought it'd be appropriate as my sixth Roald Dahl read. Now that I've read it, it's a <em>little</em> festive (gathering together with friends for a celebratory meal), but it's most likely because the film adaptation seems to always be on around Christmas – and now I cannot wait to watch it. <em>Fantastic Mr. Fox</em> is a charming, quick </span>
  <span id="freeText10267164793033300954" style="display:none"><i>This is a short blogpost taken from <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/2014/12/16/thoughts-on-roald-dahl-the-bfg-the-witches-fantastic-mr-fox/" rel="nofollow noopener">Thoughts on Roald Dahl: The BFG, The Witches &amp; Fantastic Mr. Fox</a>.</i><br /><br />I wasn't sure why, but <em>Fantastic Mr. Fox</em> felt the most <em>festive</em> to me, so I thought it'd be appropriate as my sixth Roald Dahl read. Now that I've read it, it's a <em>little</em> festive (gathering together with friends for a celebratory meal), but it's most likely because the film adaptation seems to always be on around Christmas – and now I cannot wait to watch it. <em>Fantastic Mr. Fox</em> is a charming, quick little read; a much less gruesome <em>Watership Down</em>. When three nasty men (Bean, Boggis and Bunce) put the home and lives of Mr. Fox, Mrs Fox and their four Small Foxes at risk, he comes up with an ingenious, masterful plan. It's full of smart characters – I loved the adorable four Small Foxes and their courageous determination – and it's also the first Roald Dahl book I've read, I'd say, with an obvious underlying moral message.<br /><br /><em>Mr. Fox looked at the four Small Foxes and he smiled. What fine children I have, he thought. They are starving to death and they haven't had a drink for three days, but they are still undefeated. I must not let them down.<br /></em><br /><br /><i>I also reviewed this book over on <a href="http://theprettybooks.wordpress.com/book-reviews/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pretty Books</a>.</i></span>
  <a data-text-id="10267164793033300954" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <span id="reviewTextContainer2117306683" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer11214093355562672686">So adorable. I really need to read more childrens books they are so cute. I haven´t really read anything buy Roald Dahl before so I need to catch up now. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('44oM/ujT+N9zx0AsHCEJ7E7o9FeF52DKQLxwthi4zVDZrGUsU40xt9Ts9E3r1AMzmLcTn0tq7q0bwjYH1fs/yg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('sCaYYnpDIApy2ciGgfb1ZfWsxhSveMd0RBL7HYTmdM+KAPGwwR3pYtXyfOd2A/+6I/Mh3GH1SRMfbL2sSaWGVQ==')})
  }

      <div id="aboutAuthor" class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4273.Roald_Dahl">About Roald Dahl</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
          <div class='bookAuthorProfile'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__topContainer'>
<div class='bookAuthorProfile__photoContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__widgetContainer'>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer18166351259359626395">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br/><br/>Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adv</span>
  <span id="freeText18166351259359626395" style="display:none">Roald Dahl was a British novelist, short story writer and screenwriter of Norwegian descent, who rose to prominence in the 1940's with works for both children and adults, and became one of the world's bestselling authors.<br /><br />Dahl's first published work, inspired by a meeting with C. S. Forester, was <i>Shot Down Over Libya</i>. Today the story is published as <i>A Piece of Cake</i>. The story, about his wartime adventures, was bought by the Saturday Evening Post for $900, and propelled him into a career as a writer. Its title was inspired by a highly inaccurate and sensationalized article about the crash that blinded him, which claimed he had been shot down instead of simply having to land because of low fuel.<br /><br />His first children's book was <i>The Gremlins</i>, about mischievous little creatures that were part of RAF folklore. The book was commissioned by Walt Disney for a film that was never made, and published in 1943. Dahl went on to create some of the best-loved children's stories of the 20th century, such as <i>Charlie and the Chocolate Factory</i>, <i>Matilda</i> and <i>James and the Giant Peach</i>.<br /><br />He also had a successful parallel career as the writer of macabre adult short stories, usually with a dark sense of humour and a surprise ending. Many were originally written for American magazines such as <i>Ladies Home Journal</i>, <i>Harper's</i>, <i>Playboy</i> and <i>The New Yorker</i>, then subsequently collected by Dahl into anthologies, gaining world-wide acclaim. Dahl wrote more than 60 short stories and they have appeared in numerous collections, some only being published in book form after his death. His stories also brought him three Edgar Awards: in 1954, for the collection <i>Someone Like You</i>; in 1959, for the story "The Landlady"; and in 1980, for the episode of <i>Tales of the Unexpected</i> based on "Skin".</span>
  <a data-text-id="18166351259359626395" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

</div>
</div>

      <div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/work/quotes/44775-fantastic-mr-fox">Quotes from Fantastic Mr. Fox</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
